    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3497974291" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3497974291" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10818276-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341872613p2/10818276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3497974291?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/10818276-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12779339-a-civil-campaign">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=american-authors">american-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=netgalleyreaders2020">netgalleyreaders2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=multi-character">multi-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=set-in-space">set-in-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=vorkosigan-series-challenge">vorkosigan-series-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3497974291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3355560726685004178">Most people I know who have read the Vorkosigan Saga consider this to be their favourite of the series so I had high expectations. The last book, Komarr, was basically a ‘meet cute’ between our series hero, Miles, and his new ladylove, Ekaterin. I was expecting A Civil Campaign to be a romance between the two with some sort of misunderstanding/conflict, maybe a touch of mystery for Miles to solve somewhere along the line before he wins the girl over completely.  Well… It is this story but quite </span>
  <span id="freeText3355560726685004178" style="display:none">Most people I know who have read the Vorkosigan Saga consider this to be their favourite of the series so I had high expectations. The last book, Komarr, was basically a ‘meet cute’ between our series hero, Miles, and his new ladylove, Ekaterin. I was expecting A Civil Campaign to be a romance between the two with some sort of misunderstanding/conflict, maybe a touch of mystery for Miles to solve somewhere along the line before he wins the girl over completely.  Well… It is this story but quite a bit more. <br /><br />LMB dedicates the book to an impressive list - Jane, Charlotte, Georgette, and Dorothy.  I can draw some fascinating comparisons between A Civil Campaign and their works (well, the ones I’m most familiar with -- I admit to having never read Heyer). Actually, the fact that Miles and Ekaterin’s storyline is pretty much just a homage to Sayers’s Lord Peter and Harriet Vane (who are probably my favourite book couple evah) was probably the biggest reason I was swooning over this book, and Ekaterin and Miles’s scenes in particular. I feel like I need to write a thesis to explain how a couple in a scifi book, set on another planet and in the future, are almost exactly the same as a couple who solve mysteries in a series of novels set in England in the 1920s. <br /><br />To keep it more brief though - Both Miles and Peter are considered less attractive than the women they’ve fallen for, leaving all and sundry to assume they’ve somehow used their peerage to trick their respective leading ladies into a relationship; Ekaterin and Harriet are both victims of domestic abuse where their past partners have not hit them but belittled them constantly; Miles and Peter are both mindful of the abuse and are incredibly honorable in wanting to fiercely protect Ekaterin and Harriet from slander and character assassination; instead of the typical alpha male protection though, Miles/Peter [perhaps unknowingly] give the girls a chance to recognise their inner strength and ability to fight misogyny and injustice in their own dignified and intelligent way; Miles/Peter’s wit and intelligence are what attracts these (outwardly seemingly) more attractive women; and, in the end, whilst Miles and Peter are plotting, it’s Ekaterin and Harriet who end up rescuing their beaus. <br /><br />I can also see the similarities to Austen’s books. For starters, there’s a heavy focus on family and siblings.  Besides Miles’s rocky relationship with his clone brother, Mark, the familial plots feature Ekaterin’s brother and brother-in-law’s ‘helpful’ response to her association to Miles (very Sense and Sensibility-like), the four Koudelka sisters (the daughters of the second novel Barrayar’s Kou and Drou acting very Bennet and/or Dashwood sisters-like) , and Miles’s pseudo brothers Ivan and Gregor.<br /><br />She also, like Jane and Dorothy etc, added a healthy helping of hidden feminism. There is no weak Koudelka sister, physically or mentally. Strong independent women each one, a credit to their parents, which becomes the great irony of the plot as Kou, after raising these superwomen, forgets the independence he and his wife have nurtured for so long by attempting to stifle it. One of the best scenes in the book is my beloved Cordelia pointing out the error in his judgement when it comes to Mark’s relationship with one of his girl’s (Kareen). Kou’s cry that Cordelia isn’t fighting fair with the addition of an old couch is all sorts of hilarious for those who’ve read Barrayar .<br /><br />Seriously, LMB was on point with her humour throughout this book. There’s a whole wedding proposal going awry plot point which plays out during a dinner party which, without doubt, is probably the funniest thing I’ve ever read. I am not exaggerating when I say I laughed out loud and almost had tears streaming down my face at one stage. The book is worth reading for this scene alone. (And let me just mention - slight <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ - that the reason Ekaterin rejects Miles’s wedding proposal is almost identical to the reason Harriet rejects Peter in Sayers’s books.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Besides the dinner party and couch scene, I felt like Cordelia and Aral need to be added to the great comedy duos of all time -- all their scenes are hilarious but I especially laughed at their reflections on meeting Ekaterin for the first time. There’s also Gregor’s straight faced delivery of one-liners, mostly in response to something Miles, Ivan, or Ekaterin’s son might have done. And there’s Ivan - full stop - hilarious - one of his closing scenes made me whoop with laughter (besides me yelling ‘I knew it!’). <br /><br />And I haven’t started on the butter bugs… (They’re difficult to explain, just read the thing. Or maybe a couple of the books prior to this one first. I don’t think this is one you can just pick up and understand all the humour etc without reading some of the others in the series.)<br /><br />Highly recommended obviously. Definitely a favourite. 5 out of 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="3355560726685004178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_247744884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247744884" />
    <a title="Andreea Daia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5267196-andreea-daia"><img alt="Andreea Daia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441815326p2/5267196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247744884?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Daia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Daia" href="/user/show/5267196-andreea-daia">Andreea Daia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 0671578855" href="/book/show/13497541-a-civil-campaign">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=hugo-nominee">hugo-nominee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247744884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9651638038471568773">Before I start my review I want to point out that, till this book, I thought that Ms. Bujold can do no wrong, so to speak (just check my other reviews of her books). I don't just like her writing style: I'm in LOVE with her technique. So this being said, for the last three days I've struggled to read this novel (I'm only 66% through) and, at this point, I'm almost ready to put it away and move to the next one, in hope of something more.<br/><br/>So what went wrong and what went well? (And I'm sorry, but t</span>
  <span id="freeText9651638038471568773" style="display:none">Before I start my review I want to point out that, till this book, I thought that Ms. Bujold can do no wrong, so to speak (just check my other reviews of her books). I don't just like her writing style: I'm in LOVE with her technique. So this being said, for the last three days I've struggled to read this novel (I'm only 66% through) and, at this point, I'm almost ready to put it away and move to the next one, in hope of something more.<br /><br />So what went wrong and what went well? (And I'm sorry, but this is going to be longer than my usual reviews.)<br /><br />1) There is a definite improvement in Ekaterin's character compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61884.Komarr__Vorkosigan_Saga___11_" title="Komarr (Vorkosigan Saga, #11) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Komarr</a>, probably the only good thing I have to say about this novel other than the beautiful writing. Please don't take me wrong: I take my hat off to Ms. Bujold for attempting a rare deed in the SF and Fantasy genre: to show that mothers are true heroines whom most people take for granted. Unfortunately for that good intention, Ekaterin turned out dry, while the the "chemistry" (or the lack of) between her and Miles made me yawn. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61899.A_Civil_Campaign__Vorkosigan_Saga___12_" title="A Civil Campaign (Vorkosigan Saga, #12) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">A Civil Campaign</a> brings up a more interesting Ekaterin, though from what I read so far, I still cannot call this a romance: yes, we are <i>told</i> over and over how highly Miles thinks of Ekaterin, but there is no magnetism between them and, as a reader, I simply couldn't care less if they end up together or not.<br /><br />2) If most of the previous books were occasionally funny, yet always built on a foundation of solid characters, solid plot, and heavy "messages" (without tuning the novels into a soapbox), this book is, for lack of a better word, <i>juvenile</i> (and I mean this with no disrespect to anyone who liked it). Granted, witless Ivan is still hilarious, but what happened the rest of the cast? We are supposed to deal with characters between 20 and 30+ years-old, yet with very little exceptions they demonstrate the maturity of a 12 years-old! I'm going to mention only one of Mark's lines - <i>"Last word: I win."</i><br /><br />3) Probably even more important than the previous note is the fact that there are serious inconsistencies between the assumptions of this story and the previous books. Do you remember in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61884.Komarr__Vorkosigan_Saga___11_" title="Komarr (Vorkosigan Saga, #11) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Komarr</a> when Miles and Uncle Vorthys have no problem whatsoever in sharing every single detail of their governmental secret investigation with clearance-free Aunt Vorthys, with clearance-free Ekaterin, and not only clearance-free, but terrorist-friendly Tien? Or do you remember when Uncle Vorthys tells to clearance-free Ekaterin the story of the breakout from the Cetagandan prisoner of war camp, which if publicly revealed would have been considered an act of war toward Cetaganda? Because if you remember, you must understand why it bothered me to no end that all of the sudden in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61899.A_Civil_Campaign__Vorkosigan_Saga___12_" title="A Civil Campaign (Vorkosigan Saga, #12) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">A Civil Campaign</a> ImpSec can't release the details of the terrorist act from Komarr to the Council of Counts. Let me say this again: civilian Aunt Vorthys is in the need-to-know pool for that investigation (along with civilian Cordelia and civilian Ekaterin), but not the <i>government</i> of the country?! How did this problem even pass the beta readers?<br /><br />4) I mentioned before the fact that, in my reading experience, Ms. Bujold does a spectacular job in <i>not</i> turning her books in a soapbox. Tolerance, responsibility, equality of the sexes, honor, and so on are always promoted, most often discretely if not downright surreptitiously. Regrettably <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61899.A_Civil_Campaign__Vorkosigan_Saga___12_" title="A Civil Campaign (Vorkosigan Saga, #12) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">A Civil Campaign</a> deviates from that norm by delivering repeatedly explicit lectures on one topic only: promoting women's emancipation is always a great purpose, but here this is somehow distorted into equating it with the sexual exploration. Not that I have anything against sexual discovery; but shouldn't one's personal emancipation (and I talk about both men and women) be more about about education and discovering one's identity and limits than just sex? <br /><br />5) Last Cordelia develops a serious case of parental favoritism (and questionable judgement), which in fact started in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance__Vorkosigan_Saga___9_" title="Mirror Dance (Vorkosigan Saga, #9) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror Dance</a>: Mark can do no evil, while Miles always misbehaves (even when, in my opinion, he doesn't). Do you remember her little speech from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance__Vorkosigan_Saga___9_" title="Mirror Dance (Vorkosigan Saga, #9) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror Dance</a> down these lines: <i>my dear Mark, don't worry that because of you, your brother was killed - after all nobody asked him to take that suicide mission to save your sorry butt... (of course I would have killed him if he didn't save you).</i> Well, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61899.A_Civil_Campaign__Vorkosigan_Saga___12_" title="A Civil Campaign (Vorkosigan Saga, #12) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">A Civil Campaign</a> it gets worse! Cordelia tells Miles that it was wrong to offer the woman he loved her heart's desire (to design and create a native garden) because he did it to trap her. I would be the first one to say that it was wrong to do so if he found her her work mediocre or if he didn't care about it at all. But in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61884.Komarr__Vorkosigan_Saga___11_" title="Komarr (Vorkosigan Saga, #11) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Komarr</a> he calls her work <i>"lovely,"</i> a <i>"serenity,"</i> <i>"beautiful,"</i> and he declares that she has an <i>"artist's eye"</i> for designing gardens. So why, oh why would it be wrong to ask her to create for him something that he obviously thinks the world of? (And no, he doesn't know her well enough to ask her to work for free for him! That would be utterly disrespectful.)<br /><br />You see, I consider myself a moderate feminist, although probably the scholastic term for my beliefs is <i>equality feminism</i> or <i>liberal feminism</i> (the kind that promotes equality between men and women in all domains). This being said, not only that I don't find anything insulting with Miles's "strategy," I actually think it's what I would have done if I were in his shoes. Yet, here comes mother Cordelia, who slaps him for <i>stealing Ekaterin's victory from her</i>. How can that be, when in the previous book he thought that she is entitled to that victory? <br /><br />I know that this review is three paragraphs too long, but this novel fell so short of my (granted, very high) expectations. :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="9651638038471568773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_359883677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/359883677" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/359883677?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781433207105" href="/book/show/1797903.A_Civil_Campaign">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer359883677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17835787101873516341">This one started out slowly.....FOR ME. I put that in caps as I suspect it' not true for many readers. <br/><br/>Let me explain. I'm just not a fan of romances and this is not only a romance...it's romances. There are romances of almost every imaginable type and so convoluted, complicated, confused....and so on as to satisfy any fan of romances. I on the other hand found my mind wandering and my interest waning. Oh there was a smattering of humor and the beginnings of the political intrigue we've come to </span>
  <span id="freeText17835787101873516341" style="display:none">This one started out slowly.....FOR ME. I put that in caps as I suspect it' not true for many readers. <br /><br />Let me explain. I'm just not a fan of romances and this is not only a romance...it's romances. There are romances of almost every imaginable type and so convoluted, complicated, confused....and so on as to satisfy any fan of romances. I on the other hand found my mind wandering and my interest waning. Oh there was a smattering of humor and the beginnings of the political intrigue we've come to expect when Miles is around...but nothing to really hold my interest. I was afraid that this would be the first Miles Vorkosigan novel that I'd have to give a rating of 3...or lower. Still I stayed with the book and my mind wandered in and out.<br /><br />Then when I was almost a third of the way through the novel, I found myself laughing out loud. I was to Miles' dinner party. The one where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Miles was introduced to the liveried butter bugs <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. From that point on while the aforementioned convoluted romances not only continued and for that matter became even more complex and tangled other aspects of the novel continued with them hand in hand. The humorous aspects along with the more adventurous components of the story also grew. The labyrinthine political maneuvering also came more into the fore.<br /><br />All in all in my view, the book had drawn me in. There are some good, even great humorous moments here and a good installment of Miles' life is found.<br /><br />So, while it took a while for me to get involved I did do so and give the book a 4. Those of you who actually seek out romance literature and have also loved this series up to this point will I'm sure be totally enamored with this one. <br /><br />So, I'll more than likely run down some more of these (I read this one out of order) and I still list the Vorkosigan Saga as one of the series I really enjoy.<br /><br />Think you might to...give it a chance, I can recommend this on to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17835787101873516341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3040742031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3040742031" />
    <a title="Kaa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19931478-kaa"><img alt="Kaa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539408167p2/19931478.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3040742031?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaa" href="/user/show/19931478-kaa">Kaa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781433207105" href="/book/show/1797903.A_Civil_Campaign">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19931478-kaa?shelf=wbtm-challenge">wbtm-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3040742031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3779240351552705724">Well, I've finally found a Bujold book I enjoyed. The beginning was a bit slow, and I was not very impressed with Miles's attitude toward wooing Ekaterin, but once the story got to the hilariously disastrous dinner party it started to win me over. Once Miles got his head out of his ass, I found the various romantic plotlines much more enjoyable, and I was very entertained by all of the politicking and plotting. By the end, I was laughing out loud at some of the conversations and reveals. My one </span>
  <span id="freeText3779240351552705724" style="display:none">Well, I've finally found a Bujold book I enjoyed. The beginning was a bit slow, and I was not very impressed with Miles's attitude toward wooing Ekaterin, but once the story got to the hilariously disastrous dinner party it started to win me over. Once Miles got his head out of his ass, I found the various romantic plotlines much more enjoyable, and I was very entertained by all of the politicking and plotting. By the end, I was laughing out loud at some of the conversations and reveals. My one lasting reservation was that the story doesn't seem to have a very good understanding of gender identity or sexual orientation, but for me that was more annoying than actively aggravating. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+6Uu3yLW5zI4gOFxGsBcmlxtaa+4ULldxa9rc8kpygfJWkUOCjAPpAiMqiTC/dK+LFD95Aovtw8jJjfh+YIT4Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zzyC3ue8rUXKQTMwvohZgpAtlbQHS4OaqhVLz84csMn9w+kPz1pF0/pNeGVmtdem4BAB/7U0jchMnBdd/rdpLw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer8152597425716423815">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br/><br/>Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestse</span>
  <span id="freeText8152597425716423815" style="display:none">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br /><br />Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestselling Vorkosigan Saga. Her work has been translated into over twenty languages.<br /><br />A listing of her awards and nominations may be seen here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bujold">http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bu...</a><br /> <br />A listing of her interviews is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Author_Interviews">http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Auth...</a><br /><br />An older fan-run site devoted to her work, The Bujold Nexus, is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dendarii.com/">http://www.dendarii.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
